## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and/or external driving. Classical nonlinear oscillator equations (Duffing, Van der Pol, etc.) provide the structural templates.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (damped): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Duffing oscillator (forced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (quadratic + cubic restoring)
- Nonlinear damping + forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * x**2 + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (combined model)
- Softening/hardening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order Duffing)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (nonlinear friction model)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**2 * v (cross-term nonlinearities)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillatory symmetry
- Even-power restoring forces (x²) → asymmetric potentials indicating broken symmetry
- Velocity-position product terms (v*x², v*x) → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators
- Cubic velocity terms (v³) → Rayleigh-type nonlinear dissipation limiting large-amplitude motion
- Sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) → external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Negative linear damping with positive nonlinear damping (c1*v + c2*v*x²) → limit cycle behavior (Van der Pol type)
- Sign of cubic coefficient relative to linear term → hardening spring (same sign as linear) vs softening spring (opposite sign)
- Parametric time modulation of position terms x*cos(c*t) → parametric resonance and instability regions

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `-0.583656*v*sin(x) - 1.81265*x`.

The key term is `v*sin(x)`. Let me recall the Taylor series: `sin(x) = x - x³/6 + x⁵/120 - x⁷/5040 + ...`

So `v*sin(x) = v*x - v*x³/6 + v*x⁵/120 - v*x⁷/5040 + ...`

The GT becomes: `-1.81265*x + (-0.583656)*v*(x - x³/6 + x⁵/120 - x⁷/5040 + ...)`
= `-1.81265*x - 0.583656*v*x + 0.097276*v*x³ - 0.004864*v*x⁵ + 0.000116*v*x⁷ - ...`

This is an infinite series, so no finite polynomial in x can exactly match it. However, candidates with transcendental functions (sin, exp, log) might be able to represent `sin(x)` exactly.

I need: `c0*x + c1*v*x + c2*v*x³ + c3*v*x*sin(c4*x² + c5) = -1.81265*x - 0.583656*v*sin(x)`

`sin(x) = x - x³/6 + x⁵/120 - ...` but `x*sin(c4*x² + c5)` generates different functional forms.

**Candidate 28**: `c0*x + c1*v*x + c2*v*x*sin(c3*log(c4*x² + 1) + c5)`

This has `v*x*sin(c3*log(c4*x² + 1) + c5)`. For this to equal `v*sin(x)`, we'd need `x*sin(c3*log(c4*x² + 1) + c5) = sin(x)`, which seems impossible to achieve for all x.

**Candidate 17**: `c0*x + c1*v*x + c2*v*x*exp(c3*sin(c4*x² + c5))`

Could `x*exp(c3*sin(c4*x² + c5))` represent `sin(x)`? This seems very unlikely.

Let me reconsider. None of the candidates have a bare `sin(x)` term — they all have `sin` of quadratic or logarithmic arguments, or polynomial terms in x. The function `sin(x)` cannot be exactly represented by any finite combination of `x*sin(ax² + b)`, polynomials, logs, or exponentials.

The polynomial candidates (like 9, 18, 60) would need infinite terms. Let me check the highest-order polynomial candidates:

**Candidate 3**: `c0*x + c1*v*x + c2*v*x*exp(c3*x²) + c4*v*x³ + c5*v*x⁵ + c6*v*x⁷ + c7*v*x⁹`

Here `v*x*exp(c3*x²)` = `v*x*(1 + c3*x² + c3²x⁴/2 + ...)` — this adds an infinite series but with a specific structure (exponential), not matching sin(x).

Could `exp(c3*x²)` combined with polynomial terms reproduce `sin(x)/x`? `sin(x)/x = 1 - x²/6 + x⁴/120 - ...` while `exp(c3*x²) = 1 + c3*x² + c3²x⁴/2 + ...`. The exponential has all positive higher-order coefficients (for real c3), while sin(x)/x alternates signs. Setting c3 negative gives alternating signs but the ratios between coefficients are fixed by the exponential structure and don't match those of sinc(x).

After careful analysis, none of these candidates can exactly reproduce `v*sin(x)`. **GT: -0.583656*v*sin(x) - 1.81265*x**

The key insight is that `-0.583656*v*sin(x)` can be expanded as a Taylor series:
`-0.583656*v*(x - x³/6 + x⁵/120 - x⁷/5040 + x⁹/362880 - ...)`
`= -0.583656*v*x + 0.097276*v*x³ - 0.004864*v*x⁵ + 0.000116*v*x⁷ - ...`

So the GT can be written as:
`-1.81265*x - 0.583656*v*x + 0.097276*v*x³ - 0.004864*v*x⁵ + 0.000116*v*x⁷ - ...`

This is an infinite series, so **polynomial approximations cannot be exact matches**. Only candidates that can exactly represent `v*sin(x)` (or equivalent) will match.

Let me analyze the structure: GT = `c0*x + beta*v*sin(x)` where `sin(x) = x*sin(x)/x`. The key is whether a candidate's functional form can exactly equal `v*sin(x)` for all x.

**Key functional forms to check:**

For exact match, I need candidates whose `v`-dependent part can exactly equal `v*sin(x)` and whose `v`-independent part can equal a linear function of `x`.

Let me check candidates that don't introduce non-eliminable extra terms:

**Candidates with polynomial v*x terms only** (9, 18, 33, 36, 59, 60): These are finite Taylor truncations - **NO MATCH** (can't exactly equal sin(x)).

**Candidates with log, exp terms**: `log(c*x²+1)`, `exp(c*x²)` - these are not equivalent to sin(x). **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with sin() terms**: Need to check if `sin(x)` can be reconstructed.

**Candidate 63**: `c0*x + c1*v*x + c2*v*x³ + c3*v*x*sin(c4*x² + c5)`
Need: `c1*v*x + c2*v*x³ + c3*v*x*sin(c4*x² + c5) = -0.583656*v*sin(x)`
This means `c1*x + c2*x³ + c3*x*sin(c4*x² + c5) = -0.583656*sin(x)`
The RHS is `sin(x)` which is odd. The LHS terms are all odd in x. But `x*sin(c4*x²+c5) = x*[sin(c4*x²)cos(c5) + cos(c4*x²)sin(c5)]`. This cannot reconstruct `sin(x)` exactly. **NO MATCH**.

None of the candidates contain a plain `sin(x)` or `cos(x)` term (without polynomial multiplication or argument modification). The GT requires `v*sin(x)`, but all candidates express the v-dependent part using combinations like `v*x*f(x)` where f involves polynomials, logs, exponentials, or trigonometric functions of `x²`.

Since `sin(x)/x` is not a polynomial, exponential, logarithmic function, or expressible as `sin(ax²+b)`, `log(cx²+1)`, `exp(dx²)`, or any finite combination thereof, **none of these candidates can exactly match the GT**.

Let me verify candidates with `Abs(v)`, `v²`, `v³`, `t`-dependent, `x²` terms - all introduce basis functions not in GT and can't be zeroed without losing needed terms.

After careful analysis, **no candidate can exactly reproduce `-0.583656*v*sin(x) - 1.81265*x`**.
